          <div class="Pos-r Z-0 article-container" data-template="desktop" id="article-108017306128" style="background-color:white;min-height:315px;">
           <div class="Pos-r sticky-container print-article" style="min-height:315px;">
            <div class="article-inner-container" style="max-width:1280px;">
             <div class="inset-container Mx-a">
              <div class="GridTable">
               <div class="D-tbr row-template">
                <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left">
                 <div class="content" style="width:825px;min-width:825px;">
                  <noscript>
                  </noscript>
                  <noscript>
                  </noscript>
                  <div class="GridTable grid-content">
                   <div class="D-tbr row-content">
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left Pend-20" style="width:305px;max-width:305px;">
                     <h1 class="Font-A-6-110 title W-100" id="article-aft-title-108017306128">
                      From Air-Chilled to All-Natural: Understanding Chicken Labels at the Supermarket
                     </h1>
                     <div class="attribution-component D-b W-100" id="article-aft-attribution-108017306128" style="max-width:305px;">
                      <div class="author-info author-info-text-first Pt-10 W-100 Bd-t Bd-b Bdstart-0 Bdend-0">
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t">
                          <cite class="byline col D-b Fs-n" style="padding-bottom:15px;">
                           <span class="author-name Font-C-2-140 D-b">
                            <a class="attribution-name Font-C-2-140 Fw-b Whs-n" data-ylk="t1:a2;t2:article;t3:cat;t8:79e506d0-bc90-3044-b359-a8f0eb38fd03;t9:17;elm:itm;elmt:link;itc:0" href="http://www.americastestkitchen.com/" style="color:#000;" target="_blank">
                             America's Test Kitchen
                            </a>
                           </span>
                           <time class="date Font-C-2-140 Fw-n D-b">
                            <span>
                             January 15, 2015
                            </span>
                           </time>
                          </cite>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right" style="max-width:500px;">
                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-108017306128" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <p>
                          Supermarkets used to only sell one or two types of chicken, but these days, the options available when buying whole chicken or chicken parts are overwhelming. Chickens are labeled with little explanation or clarity for the home cook. What exactly do terms like natural, organic, and air-chilled really mean?
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:79e506d0-bc90-3044-b359-a8f0eb38fd03;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://bit.ly/1u2DJ76" target="_blank">
                           <img alt="From Air-Chilled to All-Natural: Understanding Chicken Labels at the Supermarket" height="500" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/c6d5ff215d5f1e6faadbb8f944a7f3b723d9ad26.jpg" width="500"/>
                          </a>
                         </p>
                         <div>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          Many claims cited on chicken packaging have no government regulation, while those that do are often poorly enforced. Heres how to evaluate which claims are meaningfuland which are full of loopholes or empty hype.
                         </div>
                         <div>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          <strong>
                           DONT MISS:
                          </strong>
                          Browse
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:79e506d0-bc90-3044-b359-a8f0eb38fd03;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://bit.ly/1u2Dqt6" target="_blank">
                           popular chicken recipes
                          </a>
                          on
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:79e506d0-bc90-3044-b359-a8f0eb38fd03;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://bit.ly/1u2Dqt6" target="_blank">
                           CooksCountry.com
                          </a>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:79e506d0-bc90-3044-b359-a8f0eb38fd03;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://bit.ly/1u2E3mv" target="_blank">
                           <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/2d5b089d42c2525e95b9d074b601fed3282b9700.jpg" height="500" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                          </a>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          <strong>
                           USDA Organic
                          </strong>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          The seal USDA Organic is considered the gold standard for organic labeling. This label ensures that chicken eat organic feed that doesnt contain animal byproducts, are raised without antibiotics, and have access to the outdoors (how much access, however, isnt regulated).
                         </div>
                         <div>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:79e506d0-bc90-3044-b359-a8f0eb38fd03;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://bit.ly/1u2E3mv" target="_blank">
                           <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/c35aa94457f99495971c5e2873400ec46a7d9187.jpg" height="500" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                          </a>
                          <p>
                          </p>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          <strong>
                           Air-Chilled
                          </strong>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          Air-chilled means that chickens were not water-chilled en masse in a chlorinated bath and the meat did not absorb any water during processing. (Water-chilled birds can retain up to 14 percent waterwhich must be printed on the labeldiluting flavor and inflating cost.) Instead, individual chickens hang from a conveyor belt and circulate around a cold room.
                         </div>
                         <div>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          <strong>
                           WANT THE ULTIMATE RESOURCE ON COOKING MEAT &amp; POULTRY?
                          </strong>
                          The
                          <em>
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:79e506d0-bc90-3044-b359-a8f0eb38fd03;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1936493861/?tag=atkyahoo-20" target="_blank">
                            Cooks Illustrated Meat Book
                           </a>
                          </em>
                          is for you.
                         </div>
                         <div>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:79e506d0-bc90-3044-b359-a8f0eb38fd03;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://bit.ly/1u2E3mv" target="_blank">
                           <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/7f8e49dda2f5a9260347a6812355430a36698ed7.jpg" height="500" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                          </a>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          <strong>
                           Raised Without Antibiotics
                          </strong>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          Raised without antibiotics and other claims regarding antibiotic use are important; too bad theyre not strictly enforced. (The only rigorous enforcement is when the claim is subject to the USDA Organic seal.) Loopholes seem rife, like injecting the eggsnot the chickenswith antibiotics or feeding them feather meal laced with residual antibiotics from treated birds.
                         </div>
                         <div>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:79e506d0-bc90-3044-b359-a8f0eb38fd03;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://bit.ly/1u2E3mv" target="_blank">
                           <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/2d3bd69b1fef36f4d8fbbfdf471288c05e8cecf4.jpg" height="500" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                          </a>
                          <p>
                          </p>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          <strong>
                           Natural and All Natural
                          </strong>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          Beware the ubiquitous natural and all natural food labels. In actuality, the USDA has defined the term just for fresh meat, stipulating only that no synthetic substances have been added to the cut. Producers may thus raise their chickens under the most unnatural circumstances on the most unnatural diets, inject birds with broth during processing, and still put the claim on their packaging.
                         </div>
                         <div>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:79e506d0-bc90-3044-b359-a8f0eb38fd03;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://bit.ly/1u2E3mv" target="_blank">
                           <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/83620d8e656c9af57a846b281e9520264196566e.jpg" height="500" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                          </a>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          <strong>
                           Vegetarian-Fed and Vegetarian Diet
                          </strong>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          Vegetarian-fed and vegetarian diet sound healthy, but are they? Since such terms arent regulated by the government, youre relying on the producers notion of the claim, which may mean feeding chickens cheap vegetarian bakery leftovers. The winners of our whole chicken tasting assured us that their definitions mean a diet consisting of corn and soy.
                         </div>
                         <div>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          <strong>
                           Hormone-Free
                          </strong>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          When used with chicken (and pork) hormone-free is an empty reassurance, since the USDA does not allow the use of hormones or steroids in the production of either chicken or pork.
                         </div>
                         <div>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:79e506d0-bc90-3044-b359-a8f0eb38fd03;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://bit.ly/1u2E3mv" target="_blank">
                           <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/4ad3deda8a7224d3b6881160c423d496c5897305.jpg" height="282" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                          </a>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          Want more tips like these? In the
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:79e506d0-bc90-3044-b359-a8f0eb38fd03;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://bit.ly/1u2E3mv" target="_blank">
                           Chicken Purchasing and Prep
                          </a>
                          course from the
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:79e506d0-bc90-3044-b359-a8f0eb38fd03;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://bit.ly/1u2E3mv" target="_blank">
                           Americas Test Kitchen Online Cooking School
                          </a>
                          ,youll learn about chicken labeling, as what to look for when buying whole chickens or chicken parts. Youll review how best to prepare chicken for cooking, and weve included a comprehensive guide to food safety and cleanup as well.
                         </div>
                        </div>

\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EToday&#x2019;s cake is a swirly and tart lemon cheesecake baked by Kylie Antolini of \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthebakingbird.com\u002F\"\u003EThe Baking Bird\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;blog. Originally from Santa Cruz, California, Antolini is now living in Portland where she works as a dental hygienist by day. At night, she experiments in the kitchen and bakes up&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthebakingbird.com\u002Fno-bake\u002Fno-bake-chocolate-peanut-butter-oreo-tart\u002F\"\u003Eone-of-a-kind tarts\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthebakingbird.com\u002Fpie\u002Frosemary-bourbon-peach-pie\u002F\"\u003Ebeautiful pies\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthebakingbird.com\u002Fbread-recipes\u002Fsimple-banana-bread\u002F\"\u003Efresh breads\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Which brings us to her bright lemon lavender dessert.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;It&#x2019;s no secret I want to infuse practically everything I can get my hands on with lavender,&#x201D; she writes. &#x201C;With lemons being in season, everyone loving lemon in cheesecake, and the fact that lavender and lemon are a wonderful marriage of flavors, I decided to test this out.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAntolini starts by combining lemon zest and juice with sugar and eggs in a sauce pan and then cooks everything down into a thick curd. She then creates a graham cracker crust on the bottom of a springform pan and fills it with a cheesecake mixture made of ground lavender, Greek yogurt, vanilla, and cream cheese. To create the marble-like design, she spoons the lemon curd over the mixture and runs a knife through it, making yellow and white swirls. It then bakes in the oven and goes right into the fridge for four hours. The finished product? Add tofu, edamame, and &#x2014; my favorite &#x2014; avocado, and you have a totally satisfying meat-free meal.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E4 cups cooked pearl or hulled barley*\u003Cbr\u003E1 &#xBD; cups shelled, organic edamame\u003Cbr\u003E2 cups wild baby arugula\u003Cbr\u003E2 blocks savory, baked, organic tofu (firm or extra-firm), cut into &#xBE;-inch cubes\u003Cbr\u003E1 ripe avocado, halved and thinly sliced\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ELemon Tamari Dressing\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E4 tablespoons low-sodium tamari soy sauce\u003Cbr\u003E2 tablespoons toasted sesame oil\u003Cbr\u003EJuice of 1 lemon\u003Cbr\u003E1 tablespoon dried oregano\u003Cbr\u003E1 teaspoon finely grated lemon zest (optional)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn a large bowl, whisk together the tamari soy sauce, sesame oil, lemon juice, oregano, and lemon zest until well combined. Add slightly cooled cooked barley to the bowl and toss to coat.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAdd the shelled edamame and arugula and toss gently to combine. To serve, divide the barley salad among four bowls and top with tofu and avocado slices.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E*Hulled barley is barley in its most natural state, which means it needs to cook for quite a bit longer than pearl barley &#x2014;1 to 1 &#xBD; hours longer. Pearl barley has the hull removed and is therefore less tough. Adjust your cooking time based on the variety you Meal Kits Help Small Farmers Find New Ways to Distribute Food?","summary":"A horde of new, sleek, venture capital-funded services has arrived on the market peddling what they think is a solution: kits made of raw ingredients  portioned and sometimes prepped  that can be assembled quickly to make a meal from scratch.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fcf2d8a67b35ba526e60d2561d5701207687368a6.jpg\" alt=\"Can Meal Kits Help Small Farmers Find New Ways to Distribute Food?\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EA tamale kit from Luke&#x2019;s Local.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EBy Anna Roth, Civil Eats\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPutting food on the table on a busy weeknight is a universal problem. Now, a horde of new, sleek, venture capital-funded services has arrived on the market peddling what they think is a solution: kits made of raw ingredients &#x2014; portioned and sometimes prepped &#x2014; that can be assembled quickly to make a meal &#x201C;from scratch.&#x201D;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe rising popularity of these meal kits has led to a Gold Rush of sorts. Big brands like \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.blueapron.com\u002F\"\u003EBlue Apron\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.plated.com\u002F\"\u003EPlated\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.hellofresh.com\u002F\"\u003EHello Fresh\u003C\u002Fa\u003E cater to the general population, each offering a half dozen or so meal plans for everyone from families to vegetarians. Then there are the niche kits: organic food (\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Featpurely.com\u002F\"\u003EEat Purely\u003C\u002Fa\u003E), vegan food (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.thepurplecarrot.com\u002F\"\u003EThe Purple Carrot\u003C\u002Fa\u003E), Southern cooking (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.peachdish.com\u002F\"\u003EPeachDish\u003C\u002Fa\u003E), and smoothies (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fgreenblender.com\u002F\"\u003EGreen Blender\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). All claim to work with local suppliers to some extent, creating a whole new distribution outlet for small- to mid-size farms.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAlthough these kits have the potential to waste a lot of packaging, many of the companies behind them actually hope to cut down on food waste. Instead of buying obscure ingredients you&#x2019;ll only use once, or receiving three heads of kale in your weekly community supported agriculture (CSA) subscription box that will inevitably wilt in the crisper drawer, the kits provide you with only what you need for a recipe. Not a bad model for a country that throws away \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcivileats.com\u002F2014\u002F10\u002F07\u002Funcovering-americas-food-waste-fiasco\u002F\"\u003E35 million tons\u003C\u002Fa\u003E of food a year.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcivileats.com\u002F2015\u002F06\u002F25\u002Fsearching-for-food-you-can-believe-in-eat-well-guides-new-app-has-you-covered\u002F#sthash.ufXlJDnq.dpuf\"\u003EMore: Searching for Food You Can Believe in? Eat Well Guide&#x2019;s New App Has You Covered&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Ff54143c1b1ecee723b1ea581f528876397afc086.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EAn assortment of meal kits from Blue Apron.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESome meal kit creators also strive to eliminate food waste higher in the supply chain. Blue Apron claims to deliver more than 3 million meals a month. That requires a lot of produce, and Blue Apron and other services are collaborating with farmers, in some cases planning menus a year out in order to sync with crop rotations, and ensure that all the food each farm grows goes to use. In doing so, they could be creating a new form of farm-to-table food delivery, somewhere in between a CSA and a restaurant.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;We&#x2019;ve had a farm strategy since day one,&#x201D; says Matthew Wadiak, founder and COO of Blue Apron. He says that the three-year-old company has spent the past few years talking with farmers, assessing their needs and challenges, then figuring out how to address them. Wadiak is a champion of forgotten heirloom produce, like \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.highmowingseeds.com\u002Forganic-non-gmo-seeds-honey-nut-butternut-squash.html\"\u003Ehoneynut squash\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fblack%20panther%20soybeans\u002F\"\u003Eblack panther soybeans\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which he says goes over well with both his customers and the farmers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcivileats.com\u002F2015\u002F02\u002F12\u002Fis-the-online-grocery-boom-good-for-the-planet\u002F\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore: Is The Online Grocery Boom Good for the Planet?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBlue Apron works with the 31 farms, and the culinary staff have sustainable agriculture backgrounds (the culinary director came from \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.stonebarnscenter.org\u002F\"\u003EStone Barns Center for Food and Agriculture\u003C\u002Fa\u003E), so an awareness of crop rotation and cover crops has been built into their business model.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFor example, the company recently worked with 12-acre Alewife Farm farm and others nearby in New York&#x2019;s Hudson Valley to source thousands of pounds of pea shoots for a recent \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.blueapron.com\u002Frecipes\u002Fseared-wild-king-salmon-with-preserved-lemon-quinoa\"\u003Eseared salmon dish\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcivileats.com\u002F2014\u002F06\u002F16\u002Fstarting-out-a-new-farmers-first-growing-season\u002F\"\u003EAlewife owner Tyler Dennis\u003C\u002Fa\u003E says that the peas helped fix nitrogen in his soil, and the guaranteed revenue from the order was a huge boon.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcivileats.com\u002F2015\u002F02\u002F06\u002Fhow-can-we-get-america-cooking-one-crumb-at-a-time\u002F#sthash.Se8xPhyJ.dpuf\"\u003EMore:&#xA0;How Can We Get America Cooking? One Crumb at a Time\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFarmers are not only reliant on the weather, but also on the whims of customers at farmers&#x2019; markets and the picky palates of chefs to sell their wares. Dennis is talking with the company to grow more peas, as well as some baby fennel and baby leeks. &#x201C;I would really like to incorporate my business with Blue Apron&#x2019;s in a more substantial way,&#x201D; he says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThese meal kits can be expensive when compared to a home-cooked meal at around $8 and $12 per person. That&#x2019;s not much more than take-out from most casual restaurants, but they do require 10-30 minutes of actual cooking time. They also create their own waste in the form of the packaging that holds, say, two tablespoons of butter for one recipe, or the ice packs to keep the food cold. But meal kit proponents are quick to point out that they&#x2019;re also eliminating a lot of the packaging higher up in the food distribution stream.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore: An App for That: Technology as a Solution to Our Broken Food System?&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPerhaps the most limiting part, at least to someone who knows how to cook, is that these services only offer a few options each day. That&#x2019;s where a model more like \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Flukeslocal.com\u002F\"\u003ELuke&#x2019;s Local\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, a San Francisco-based meal delivery company, comes in. Its stated goal is to help busy people get through the week. So the business offers recipe kits, but also heat-and-serve prepared meals and raw produce and ingredients, more like a regular CSA.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;[Our customers] love that they can get some of these things to cook dinner or have dinner at home, some fruit for the morning for breakfast, a box lunch to bring to work,&#x201D; says owner Luke Chappell.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcivileats.com\u002F2014\u002F11\u002F17\u002Ftoss-those-take-out-menus-new-study-says-cooking-makes-us-healthier\u002F#sthash.Il10pdyd.dpuf\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore: Toss Those Take-Out Menus: New Study Says Cooking Makes us Healthier\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELike Wadiak, Chappell has made working with farmers a priority from the beginning. He says that there&#x2019;s rarely a day that goes by without communication between his team of chefs and farmers like Andy Griffin from Watsonville&#x2019;s \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.mariquita.com\u002F\"\u003EMariquita Farm\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x2014;either they&#x2019;re on the phone talking about what&#x2019;s fresh that week, or Griffin is texting them photos of what&#x2019;s ripe and good to feature. In a weekly meeting, the team looks at all the produce set to come in and figures out what to do with it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOffering a range of options also eliminates waste almost entirely, says Chappell. For example, he can source a whole pig from Chico, California-based \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fllanoseco.com\u002F\"\u003ELlano Seco Ranch\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and use every part: the skin for chicharones, the bones for broth, the cuts for the prepared chefs meals, chorizo for a breakfast burrito, and tenderloins for a dinner recipe kit.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcivileats.com\u002F2013\u002F10\u002F14\u002Fcooking-as-the-cornerstone-of-a-sustainable-food-system\u002F#sthash.VVJ03odz.dpuf\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003ECooking as the Cornerstone of a Sustainable Food System\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFood gurus like Michael Pollan and Mark Bittman often point to scratch cooking as \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftime.com\u002F3483888\u002Fthe-truth-about-home-cooking\u002F\"\u003Ethe answer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E to many of \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2009\u002F08\u002F02\u002Fmagazine\u002F02cooking-t.html?pagewanted=all&amp;_r=0\"\u003Eour food system&#x2019;s ills\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and the best a way to eat sustainably grown ingredients without breaking the bank. But it&#x2019;s unclear whether or not meal kits can ever serve as a bridge to more affordable, traditional home cooking.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThey could simply be a function of the new &#x201C;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmedium.com\u002Fondemand\u002Fthe-shut-in-economy-ec3ec1294816\"\u003Eshut in economy\u003C\u002Fa\u003E,&#x201D; where those with means order everything into their homes and never leave. But those behind the companies say they&#x2019;re working to make it easier for busy professionals and families, who might not cook at all otherwise, to take advantage of the values of community supported agriculture or farmers&#x2019; market shopping without the time commitment.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;My argument is that we take the good parts of the CSA, which is the seasonality, but we make it really usable for everybody,&#x201D; says Wadiak. And no matter how you feel about the cooking-by-the-numbers approach to dinner, it&#x2019;s hard to argue with that.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore food for thought from Yahoo Drinks That Do (and Taste) Good\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca Chickens are labeled with little explanation or clarity for the home cook. What exactly do terms like &#x201C;natural,&#x201D; &#x201C;organic,&#x201D; and &#x201C;air-chilled&#x201D; really mean?&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fbit.ly\u002F1u2DJ76\"\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"From Air-Chilled to All-Natural: Understanding Chicken Labels at the Supermarket\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fc6d5ff215d5f1e6faadbb8f944a7f3b723d9ad26.jpg\" width=\"500\" height=\"500\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n Many claims cited on chicken packaging have no government regulation, while those that do are often poorly enforced. Here&#x2019;s how to evaluate which claims are meaningful&#x2014;and which are full of loopholes or empty hype.\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Cstrong\u003EDON&#x2019;T MISS:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003EBrowse \n \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fbit.ly\u002F1u2Dqt6\"\u003Epopular chicken recipes\u003C\u002Fa\u003E on \n \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fbit.ly\u002F1u2Dqt6\"\u003ECooksCountry.com\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fbit.ly\u002F1u2E3mv\"\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"500\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F2d5b089d42c2525e95b9d074b601fed3282b9700.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E \n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Cstrong\u003EUSDA Organic\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n The seal &#x201C;USDA Organic&#x201D; is considered the gold standard for organic labeling. This label ensures that chicken eat organic feed that doesn&#x2019;t contain animal byproducts, are raised without antibiotics, and have access to the outdoors (how much access, however, isn&#x2019;t regulated).\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fbit.ly\u002F1u2E3mv\"\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"500\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fc35aa94457f99495971c5e2873400ec46a7d9187.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Cstrong\u003EAir-Chilled\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n &#x201C;Air-chilled&#x201D; means that chickens were not water-chilled en masse in a chlorinated bath and the meat did not absorb any water during processing. (Water-chilled birds can retain up to 14 percent water&#x2014;which must be printed on the label&#x2014;diluting flavor and inflating cost.) Instead, individual chickens hang from a conveyor belt and circulate around a cold room.\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Cstrong\u003EWANT THE ULTIMATE RESOURCE ON COOKING MEAT &amp; POULTRY?&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003EThe \n \u003Cem\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.amazon.com\u002Fgp\u002Fproduct\u002F1936493861\u002F?tag=atkyahoo-20\"\u003ECook&#x2019;s Illustrated Meat Book\u003C\u002Fa\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eis for you.\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fbit.ly\u002F1u2E3mv\"\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"500\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F7f8e49dda2f5a9260347a6812355430a36698ed7.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E \n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Cstrong\u003ERaised Without Antibiotics\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n &#x201C;Raised without antibiotics&#x201D; and other claims regarding antibiotic use are important; too bad they&#x2019;re not strictly enforced. (The only rigorous enforcement is when the claim is subject to the USDA Organic seal.) Loopholes seem rife, like injecting the eggs&#x2014;not the chickens&#x2014;with antibiotics or feeding them feather meal laced with residual antibiotics from treated birds.\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fbit.ly\u002F1u2E3mv\"\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"500\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F2d3bd69b1fef36f4d8fbbfdf471288c05e8cecf4.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Cstrong\u003ENatural and All Natural\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n Beware the ubiquitous &#x201C;natural&#x201D; and &#x201C;all natural&#x201D; food labels. In actuality, the USDA has defined the term just for fresh meat, stipulating only that no synthetic substances have been added to the cut. Producers may thus raise their chickens under the most unnatural circumstances on the most unnatural diets, inject birds with broth during processing, and still put the claim on their packaging.\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fbit.ly\u002F1u2E3mv\"\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"500\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F83620d8e656c9af57a846b281e9520264196566e.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E \n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Cstrong\u003EVegetarian-Fed and Vegetarian Diet\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n &#x201C;Vegetarian-fed&#x201D; and &#x201C;vegetarian diet&#x201D; sound healthy, but are they? Since such terms aren&#x2019;t regulated by the government, you&#x2019;re relying on the producer&#x2019;s notion of the claim, which may mean feeding chickens cheap &#x201C;vegetarian&#x201D; bakery leftovers. The winners of our whole chicken tasting assured us that their definitions mean a diet consisting of corn and soy.\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Cstrong\u003EHormone-Free\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n When used with chicken (and pork) &#x201C;hormone-free&#x201D; is an empty reassurance, since the USDA does not allow the use of hormones or steroids in the production of either chicken or pork.\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fbit.ly\u002F1u2E3mv\"\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"282\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F4ad3deda8a7224d3b6881160c423d496c5897305.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n Want more tips like these?
